Government and politics {#Government_and_politics}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Government and politics")\]  
Further information: [Politics of Afghanistan](/wiki/Politics_of_Afghanistan "Politics of Afghanistan")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/200229-D-AP390-1529_%2849603221753%29.jpg/200px-200229-D-AP390-1529_%2849603221753%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:200229-D-AP390-1529_(49603221753).jpg) [Arg](/wiki/Arg_(Kabul) "Arg (Kabul)"), the Presidential Palace in Kabul

The municipality's administrative structure consisted of 17 departments under a [mayor](/wiki/Mayor "Mayor"). Like other provincial municipalities in Afghanistan, the municipality of Kabul dealt with city affairs such as construction and infrastructure. The city districts (*nāhia* ) collected certain taxes and issued building licenses. Each city district had a district head appointed by the mayor, and lead six major departments in the district office. The neighbourhood organisation structure at the *nahia* level was called a *gozar* . Kabul has been Divided in to 630 Gozars. A *wakil-e gozar* was a person chosen to represent a community within a city district.

Kabul's Chief of Police was Lt. Gen. Abdul Rahman Rahimi. The police were part of the [Afghan National Police](/wiki/Afghan_National_Police "Afghan National Police") (ANP) under the [Ministry of Interior](/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Interior_(Afghanistan) "Ministry of the Interior (Afghanistan)") and were arranged by city districts. The Police Chief was selected by the Interior Minister and is responsible for all [law enforcement](/wiki/Law_enforcement "Law enforcement") activities throughout the Kabul province.  

Economy and infrastructure {#Economy_and_infrastructure}
--------------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Economy and infrastructure")\]  
Further information: [Economy of Afghanistan](/wiki/Economy_of_Afghanistan "Economy of Afghanistan")

Kabul's main products included [fresh](/wiki/Fruit "Fruit") and [dried fruit](/wiki/Dried_fruit "Dried fruit"), [nuts](/wiki/Nut_(fruit) "Nut (fruit)"), beverages, [Afghan rugs](/wiki/Afghan_rug "Afghan rug"), [leather](/wiki/Leather "Leather") and sheep skin products, furniture, [antique](/wiki/Antique "Antique") [replicas](/wiki/Replica "Replica"), and domestic clothes. The [World Bank](/wiki/World_Bank "World Bank") authorised [US$](/wiki/United_States_dollar "United States dollar")25 million for the Kabul Urban Reconstruction Project which closed in 2011.^[\[165\]](#cite_note-166)^ Over the last decade, the United States has invested approximately $9.1 billion into urban infrastructure in Afghanistan.^[\[166\]](#cite_note-167)^^[\[167\]](#cite_note-wsj-168)^ [The wars since 1978](/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(1978%E2%80%93present) "War in Afghanistan (1978–present)") have limited the city's economic productivity but after the establishment of the Karzai administration since late 2001, local economic developments have included a number of [indoor shopping malls](/wiki/Indoor_shopping_mall "Indoor shopping mall"). The first of these was the [Kabul City Center](/wiki/Kabul_City_Center "Kabul City Center"), opened 2005. Others have also opened in recent years including [Gulbahar Center](/w/index.php?title=Gulbahar_Center&action=edit&redlink=1 "Gulbahar Center (page does not exist)"), [City Walk Mall](/w/index.php?title=City_Walk_Mall&action=edit&redlink=1 "City Walk Mall (page does not exist)") and [Majid Mall](/w/index.php?title=Majid_Mall&action=edit&redlink=1 "Majid Mall (page does not exist)").^[\[168\]](#cite_note-169)^{#cite_ref-169}

Mandawi Road on the south side of the river, located between Murad Khani and Shur Bazaar neighbourhoods, is one of the main bazaars of Kabul. This wholesale market is very popular amongst locals. Nearby is the Sarai Shahzada money exchange market.^[\[169\]](#cite_note-170)^ [Chicken Street](/wiki/Chicken_Street "Chicken Street") is perhaps best known to foreigners.^[\[170\]](#cite_note-171)^{#cite_ref-171}

Kabul's largest industrial hub was located in District 9, on the north banks of the River Kabul and near the airport.^[\[147\]](#cite_note-iwaweb.org-148)^ About 6 km (4 mi) from downtown Kabul, in [Bagrami](/wiki/Bagrami_District "Bagrami District"), a 9-hectare (22-acre) industrial complex had been completed with modern facilities, which allowed companies to operate businesses there. The park had professional management for the daily maintenance of public roads, internal streets, common areas, parking areas, 24 hours perimeter security, access control for vehicles and people.^[\[171\]](#cite_note-172)^ A number of factories operated there, including the $25 million Coca-Cola bottling plant and the Omaid Bahar juice factory.{#cite_ref-172}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kabul_Antiquity_Shop2.jpg/200px-Kabul_Antiquity_Shop2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kabul_Antiquity_Shop2.jpg) Inside an antiquity shop in Kabul's famous [Chicken Street](/wiki/Chicken_Street "Chicken Street") (*Kochi Murgha*)

According to [Transparency International](/wiki/Transparency_International "Transparency International"), the government of Afghanistan was the third most-[corrupt](/wiki/Corruption "Corruption") in the world, as of 2010.^[\[172\]](#cite_note-TI-173)^ Experts believe that the poor decisions of Afghan politicians contributed to the unrest in the region. This also prevented foreign investment in Afghanistan, especially by Western countries. In 2012, there were reportedly $3.9 billion paid to public officials in [bribes](/wiki/Bribery "Bribery") which contributed to these issues.^[\[173\]](#cite_note-174)^{#cite_ref-174}

[Da Afghanistan Bank](/wiki/Da_Afghanistan_Bank "Da Afghanistan Bank"), the nation's [central bank](/wiki/Central_bank "Central bank"), was headquartered in Kabul. In addition, there are several commercial banks in the city.^[\[174\]](#cite_note-175)^{#cite_ref-175}

As of 2016 there were^\[*[needs update?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")*\]^ about 20,000 foreign tourists visiting Afghanistan per year.^[\[175\]](#cite_note-176)^{#cite_ref-176}  

### Development planning {#Development_planning}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Development planning")\]

A US$1 billion contract was signed in 2013 to commence work on the "Kabul New City" (sometimes reported as "New Kabul City"), which is a major residential scheme that would accommodate 1.5 million people.^[\[176\]](#cite_note-177)^^[\[177\]](#cite_note-178)^^[\[178\]](#cite_note-179)^^[\[179\]](#cite_note-180)^ Construction was delayed due to instability in the region, but construction broke ground in August 2023 after a new contract was signed between the Ministry of Urban Development and Housing and Khawar Company. The new agreement is expected to modernize the city, address overpopulation, and incentivize the return of [expatriates](/wiki/Expatriate "Expatriate") by adding housing to accommodate 3 million people and modern amenities.^[\[180\]](#cite_note-181)^^[\[181\]](#cite_note-182)^^[\[182\]](#cite_note-183)^ The construction is planned to occur in two phases over the span of about 30 years.{#cite_ref-183}

Another development is the Qatar Township in Kabul.^[\[183\]](#cite_note-184)^ Construction was halted for the COVID-19 pandemic, but resumed in May 2023. The township---which is planned to include 12 blocks with 768 flats, three business blocks, one mosque, two schools, and an orphanage---could become operational in 2024.^[\[184\]](#cite_note-185)^{#cite_ref-185}  

### Communications {#Communications}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Communications")\]  
Further information: [Communications in Afghanistan](/wiki/Communications_in_Afghanistan "Communications in Afghanistan")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/1950s_Afghanistan_-_Afghan_radio_station.jpg/200px-1950s_Afghanistan_-_Afghan_radio_station.jpg)](/wiki/File:1950s_Afghanistan_-_Afghan_radio_station.jpg) Studio of [Radio Kabul](/wiki/Radio_Kabul "Radio Kabul") in the 1950s

As of November 2015, there were more than 24 television stations based out of Kabul.^[\[185\]](#cite_note-186)^ Terrestrial TV transmitters were located at the summit of the [Koh-e Asamai](/wiki/Koh-e_Asamai "Koh-e Asamai").{#cite_ref-186}

[GSM](/wiki/GSM "GSM")/[GPRS](/wiki/GPRS "GPRS") mobile phone services are provided by [Afghan Wireless](/wiki/Afghan_Wireless "Afghan Wireless"), [Etisalat](/wiki/Etisalat "Etisalat"), [Roshan](/wiki/Roshan_(Telecom) "Roshan (Telecom)"), [MTN](/wiki/MTN_Group "MTN Group") and [Salaam](/w/index.php?title=Salaam_(mobile_carrier)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Salaam (mobile carrier) (page does not exist)"). They provide [4G](/wiki/4G "4G") and [3G](/wiki/3G "3G") services. In November 2006, the [Afghan Ministry of Communications](/wiki/Afghan_Ministry_of_Communications "Afghan Ministry of Communications") signed a US$64.5 million deal with [ZTE](/wiki/ZTE "ZTE") on the establishment of a countrywide fibre optical cable network to help improve telephone, internet, television and radio broadcast services not just in Kabul but throughout the country.

Mail and delivery services are provided by [Afghan Post](/wiki/Afghan_Post "Afghan Post"), [FedEx](/wiki/FedEx "FedEx"), [TNT N.V.](/wiki/TNT_N.V. "TNT N.V."), and [DHL](/wiki/DHL_Express "DHL Express").  

### Hotels and other lodging {#Hotels_and_other_lodging}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Hotels and other lodging")\]  
Further information: [Tourism in Afghanistan](/wiki/Tourism_in_Afghanistan "Tourism in Afghanistan")

Kabul has many hotels for domestic and foreign travelers. [Guest houses](/wiki/Guest_house "Guest house") are also found in the city. The better and safer ones are located in the [Shahr-e Naw](/wiki/Shahr-e_Naw "Shahr-e Naw") and [Wazir Akbar Khan](/wiki/Wazir_Akbar_Khan,_Kabul "Wazir Akbar Khan, Kabul") neighbourhoods (the Green Zone). The following are some of the hotels in Kabul (in alphabetical order).

* Baron Hotel
* Central Hotel
* Darya Village Hotel
* Golden Star Hotel
* [Kabul Inter-Continental](/wiki/Hotel_Inter-Continental_Kabul "Hotel Inter-Continental Kabul")
* [Kabul Serena Hotel](/wiki/Kabul_Serena_Hotel "Kabul Serena Hotel")
* Kabul Star Hotel
* Khyber Hotel
* Park Star Hotel
* [Safi Landmark Hotel](/wiki/Safi_Landmark_Hotel "Safi Landmark Hotel")
* Spinzar Hotel
* Zohak Village

Culture and landmarks {#Culture_and_landmarks}
----------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Culture and landmarks")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Bird_Market_Kabul.jpg/220px-Bird_Market_Kabul.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bird_Market_Kabul.jpg) The Kabul Bird Market (*Ka Foroshi*)

The old part of Kabul was filled with [bazaars](/wiki/Bazaar "Bazaar") nestled along its narrow, crooked streets, examples being the Mandawi and the Bird Market (*Ka Foroshi* ). Cultural sites included: the [National Museum of Afghanistan](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Afghanistan "National Museum of Afghanistan"), notably displaying an impressive statue of [Surya](/wiki/Surya "Surya") excavated at [Khair Khana](/wiki/Khair_Khana "Khair Khana"), the ruined [Darul Aman Palace](/wiki/Darul_Aman_Palace "Darul Aman Palace"), the tomb of Mughal Emperor [Babur](/wiki/Babur "Babur") at [Bagh-e Babur](/wiki/Bagh-e_Babur "Bagh-e Babur"), and Chihil Sutun Park, the Minar-i-Istiqlal (Column of Independence) built in 1919 after the [Third Afghan War](/wiki/Third_Afghan_War "Third Afghan War"), the [tomb of Timur Shah Durrani](/wiki/Tomb_of_Timur_Shah_Durrani "Tomb of Timur Shah Durrani"), the [Bagh-e Bala Palace](/wiki/Bagh-e_Bala_Palace "Bagh-e Bala Palace") and the imposing [Id Gah Mosque](/wiki/Id_Gah_Mosque "Id Gah Mosque") (founded 1893). [Bala Hissar](/wiki/Bala_Hissar,_Kabul "Bala Hissar, Kabul") was a fort which was partially destroyed during the [Second Anglo-Afghan War](/wiki/Second_Anglo-Afghan_War "Second Anglo-Afghan War"),^[\[62\]](#cite_note-lib-63)^ then restored as a military college. There was also the [Kolola Pushta](/w/index.php?title=Kolola_Pushta&action=edit&redlink=1 "Kolola Pushta (page does not exist)") fort, which was garrisoned by the Afghan Army, and the nearby 19th-century [Shahrara Tower](/w/index.php?title=Shahrara_Tower&action=edit&redlink=1 "Shahrara Tower (page does not exist)") fort, which was ruined in 1928. The [Koh-e Asamai](/wiki/Koh-e_Asamai "Koh-e Asamai") mountain had a temple that was considered important to [Hinduism](/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism").{#cite_ref-lib_63-1}

Other places of interest include [Kabul City Center](/wiki/Kabul_City_Center "Kabul City Center"), which was Kabul's first shopping mall, the shops around Flower Street and [Chicken Street](/wiki/Chicken_Street "Chicken Street"), Wazir Akbar Khan district, [Kabul Golf Club](/wiki/Kabul_Golf_Club "Kabul Golf Club"), [Kabul Zoo](/wiki/Kabul_Zoo "Kabul Zoo"), [Abdul Rahman Mosque](/wiki/Abdul_Rahman_Mosque "Abdul Rahman Mosque"), [Shah-Do Shamshira](/wiki/Shah-Do_Shamshira_Mosque "Shah-Do Shamshira Mosque") and other famous mosques, the [National Gallery of Afghanistan](/w/index.php?title=National_Gallery_of_Afghanistan&action=edit&redlink=1 "National Gallery of Afghanistan (page does not exist)"), the [National Archives of Afghanistan](/wiki/National_Archives_of_Afghanistan "National Archives of Afghanistan"), Afghan Royal Family Mausoleum, the [OMAR Mine Museum](/wiki/OMAR_Mine_Museum "OMAR Mine Museum"), Bibi Mahro Hill, Kabul Cemetery, and [Paghman Gardens](/wiki/Paghman_Gardens "Paghman Gardens") best known for the famous [Taq-e Zafar](/wiki/Taq-e_Zafar "Taq-e Zafar") arch. The Aga Khan Development Network (AKDN) was also involved in the restoration of the [Bagh-e Babur](/wiki/Bagh-e_Babur "Bagh-e Babur") (Babur Gardens).

Maranjan Hill (*Tappe-i-Maranjan* ) was a nearby hill where Buddhist [statues](/wiki/Statue "Statue") and Graeco-Bactrian [coins](/wiki/Coin "Coin") from the 2nd century BC have been found. Outside the city proper lied the Buddhist [Guldara stupa](/wiki/Guldara_stupa "Guldara stupa") and another stupa at [Shewaki](/wiki/Shewaki "Shewaki"). [Paghman](/wiki/Paghman "Paghman") and [Jalalabad](/wiki/Jalalabad "Jalalabad") were interesting valleys west and east of the city. On the latter road, about 16 miles east of the city, was the [Tang-e Gharu](/wiki/Tang-e_Gharu "Tang-e Gharu") gorge.

Kabul used to have as many as 23 cinemas, but currently only had four, including the state owned [Ariana Cinema](/wiki/Ariana_Cinema "Ariana Cinema"). The decline of [cinema of Afghanistan](/wiki/Cinema_of_Afghanistan "Cinema of Afghanistan") since the 1990s, both due to war and oppressive regimes, had meant many of these have closed.^[\[186\]](#cite_note-tolonews.com-187)^ The Nandari, or Kabul National Theater, was one of the largest theaters in Asia before it was destroyed in the civil war and has not been restored.^[\[187\]](#cite_note-188)^ The lack of investment meant that the sector did not recover after 2001, and notably the rundown Park Cinema was controversially demolished in 2020.^[\[186\]](#cite_note-tolonews.com-187)^{#cite_ref-tolonews.com_187-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Kabul%27s_national_history_museum.jpg/220px-Kabul%27s_national_history_museum.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kabul%27s_national_history_museum.jpg) [National Museum of Afghanistan](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Afghanistan "National Museum of Afghanistan") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/National_Archives%2C_Afghanistan.jpg/220px-National_Archives%2C_Afghanistan.jpg)](/wiki/File:National_Archives,_Afghanistan.jpg) Afghanistan National Archives [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Bebi_Mahroo_Park_in_2010.jpg/220px-Bebi_Mahroo_Park_in_2010.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bebi_Mahroo_Park_in_2010.jpg) Bibi Mahro Park

  * [Bagh-e Chihil Sutun](/wiki/Chihil_Sutun "Chihil Sutun") (Gardens of [Chihil Sutun](/wiki/Chihil_Sutun "Chihil Sutun"))
  * Bagh-e Bala Park

  * Bagh-e Zanana
  * [Chaman-e-Hozori](/wiki/Chaman-e-Hozori "Chaman-e-Hozori")

  * [Lake Qargha](/wiki/Lake_Qargha "Lake Qargha")
* **Mosques**

  * [Sakhi Shrine](/wiki/Sakhi_Shrine "Sakhi Shrine")

  * Mausoleum of [Zahir Shah](/wiki/Mohammed_Zahir_Shah "Mohammed Zahir Shah"), [Nadir Shah](/wiki/Mohammed_Nadir_Khan "Mohammed Nadir Khan") and other members of the royal [Musahiban](/wiki/Musahiban "Musahiban") family
  * Mausoleum of [Jamal-al-Din al-Afghani](/wiki/Jamal-al-Din_al-Afghani "Jamal-al-Din al-Afghani")
* **Palaces**
  * [Tajbeg Palace](/wiki/Tajbeg_Palace "Tajbeg Palace")
  * [Stor Palace](/w/index.php?title=Stor_Palace&action=edit&redlink=1 "Stor Palace (page does not exist)")
  * [Darul Aman Palace](/wiki/Darul_Aman_Palace "Darul Aman Palace")
  * [Chihil Sutun Palace](/wiki/Chihil_Sutun_Palace "Chihil Sutun Palace")
  * [Bagh-e Bala Palace](/wiki/Bagh-e_Bala_Palace "Bagh-e Bala Palace")
  * [Shah Bobo Jan Palace](/w/index.php?title=Shah_Bobo_Jan_Palace&action=edit&redlink=1 "Shah Bobo Jan Palace (page does not exist)")
  * [Arg (Presidential Palace)](/wiki/Arg_(Kabul) "Arg (Kabul)"), including numerous other palaces inside the compound
    * [Char Chenar Palace](/w/index.php?title=Char_Chenar_Palace&action=edit&redlink=1 "Char Chenar Palace (page does not exist)")
    * [Delgusha Palace](/w/index.php?title=Delgusha_Palace&action=edit&redlink=1 "Delgusha Palace (page does not exist)") and its [clock tower](/wiki/Clock_tower "Clock tower")
    * [Haram Sara Palace](/w/index.php?title=Haram_Sara_Palace&action=edit&redlink=1 "Haram Sara Palace (page does not exist)")
    * [Salam Khana Palace](/w/index.php?title=Salam_Khana_Palace&action=edit&redlink=1 "Salam Khana Palace (page does not exist)")

* **Museums**

* **Other landmarks**
  * Clock tower at Mahmoud Khan Bridge
  * Minaret of Knowledge and Ignorance
  * Minaret of the Unknown Corps on [Jada-e Maiwand](/wiki/Jada-e_Maiwand "Jada-e Maiwand")
  * [Sherpur Cantonment](/wiki/Sherpur_Cantonment "Sherpur Cantonment") (British Cemetery)

### Architecture {#Architecture}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Architecture")\]  
See also: [Architecture of Afghanistan](/wiki/Architecture_of_Afghanistan "Architecture of Afghanistan")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Shah_Do_Shamshira_aerial.png/220px-Shah_Do_Shamshira_aerial.png)](/wiki/File:Shah_Do_Shamshira_aerial.png) Italian baroque style of Shah Do Shamshira

Kabul's various architectural designs reflected the various links it has had with empires and civilisations, particularly being on the ancient trade route connecting India and China with Persia and the West.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-Architectural-190)^{#cite_ref-Architectural_190-0}

The Buddhist [Chakari minaret](/wiki/Chakari,_Afghanistan "Chakari, Afghanistan") was likely built in the [Kushan](/wiki/Kushan_Empire "Kushan Empire") era and had traces of [Greco-Bactrian](/wiki/Greco-Bactrian "Greco-Bactrian") and [Gandhara Art](/wiki/Gandhara_Art "Gandhara Art"). It had Buddhist [swastika](/wiki/Swastika "Swastika") and both [Mahayana](/wiki/Mahayana "Mahayana") and [Theravada](/wiki/Theravada "Theravada") qualities. Following the Islamic conquest, a new age of architectural realms appeared in the Kabul region. The [Gardens of Babur](/wiki/Gardens_of_Babur "Gardens of Babur") was perhaps the best preserved example of Islamic and [Mughal](/wiki/Mughal_architecture "Mughal architecture") architecture. Emperor [Babur](/wiki/Babur "Babur") had also built seven other big gardens in Kabul at the time. The present Gardens of Babur also reflect Afghanistan's traditional architecture by the wooden carving, pressed stucco, decorative stone masonry and other features. Another fine example of the Babur era is the [Id Gah Mosque](/wiki/Id_Gah_Mosque "Id Gah Mosque"), using stones from the [Punjab](/wiki/Punjab "Punjab") and [Sindh](/wiki/Sindh "Sindh") and designed by Persians.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-Architectural-190)^{#cite_ref-Architectural_190-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/The_Mausoleum_of_Timur_Shah%2C_Kabul%2C_1879.jpg/220px-The_Mausoleum_of_Timur_Shah%2C_Kabul%2C_1879.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Mausoleum_of_Timur_Shah,_Kabul,_1879.jpg) [Tomb of Timur Shah Durrani](/wiki/Tomb_of_Timur_Shah_Durrani "Tomb of Timur Shah Durrani") (early 19th century rebuilt)

[Ahmad Shah Durrani](/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Durrani "Ahmad Shah Durrani")'s rise as the Afghan ruler brought changes to Kabul and the nation, with a more inward-looking and self-protecting society reflecting the architecture that were no different between the rich and poor peoples. mausoleum of [Timur Shah Durrani](/wiki/Timur_Shah_Durrani "Timur Shah Durrani"), the Afghan ruler until his death in 1793, was another example of Islamic design, built in an octagonal structure. It followed [Central Asian](/wiki/Central_Asian "Central Asian") traditions of decorative brick masonries along with a colorless appearance.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-Architectural-190)^ After the [Second Anglo-Afghan War](/wiki/Second_Anglo-Afghan_War "Second Anglo-Afghan War"), the country's emir [Abdur Rahman Khan](/wiki/Abdur_Rahman_Khan "Abdur Rahman Khan") brought European styles for the first time. The [Bagh-e Bala Palace](/wiki/Bagh-e_Bala_Palace "Bagh-e Bala Palace") was designed in a mixed Mughal and British Indian style, the first significant change from traditional Afghan and Islamic styles. However, palaces were still built with Central Asian Islamic design at heart. Numerous lavish buildings were created during this time, combined with large gardens. The Dilkusha Palace within the [Arg](/wiki/Arg_(Kabul) "Arg (Kabul)") was the first created by a British architect.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-Architectural-190)^ Its accompanying [clock tower](/wiki/Clock_tower "Clock tower"),  1911, was also a British creation.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-191)^{#cite_ref-191}

Houses in Kabul during this time were generally made up of walled compounds, built around courtyards and having narrow passageways to places.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-ReutersHomes-192)^{#cite_ref-ReutersHomes_192-0}

In the 1920s, new styles were strongly influenced by European architectural styles due to king [Amanullah Khan](/wiki/Amanullah_Khan "Amanullah Khan")'s visits to Europe, particularly Berlin and Paris. [Darul Aman Palace](/wiki/Darul_Aman_Palace "Darul Aman Palace") was the best known example of modern Western design. The [Shah-Do Shamshira Mosque](/wiki/Shah-Do_Shamshira_Mosque "Shah-Do Shamshira Mosque") was built in an unusual style for a mosque in Western and Italian style [baroque](/wiki/Baroque "Baroque"). The [Taq-e Zafar](/wiki/Taq-e_Zafar "Taq-e Zafar") in [Paghman](/wiki/Paghman "Paghman") and other landmarks there were also based on European designs.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-Architectural-190)^ Houses also became more open, without having many of the walls.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-ReutersHomes-192)^ Later in the century, several [Soviet](/wiki/Soviet "Soviet") inspired designs made its way into Kabul. Most notable of these were the various *[microraion](/wiki/Microraion "Microraion")* s built in the city in the 1960s and afterwards. A different flavor of modern style was seen on the [Hotel Inter-Continental Kabul](/wiki/Hotel_Inter-Continental_Kabul "Hotel Inter-Continental Kabul") and [Serena Hotel](/wiki/Kabul_Serena_Hotel "Kabul Serena Hotel").^[\[189\]](#cite_note-Architectural-190)^{#cite_ref-Architectural_190-5}

In the 21st century, modern designs based on glass facades became popular. Examples of this modern Western style were the [Kabul City Center](/wiki/Kabul_City_Center "Kabul City Center") and [Golbahar Center](/w/index.php?title=Golbahar_Center&action=edit&redlink=1 "Golbahar Center (page does not exist)"). The [National Assembly](/wiki/National_Assembly_(Afghanistan) "National Assembly (Afghanistan)") building opened in 2015 had elements of modern Islamic [Mughal](/wiki/Mughal_architecture "Mughal architecture") architecture, considered to have the largest dome in Asia. The Indian architecture could also be influenced by the fact it was built by the government of India, but its carving and large porch represent Afghan traditional architectural forms.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-Architectural-190)^ The new [Ministry of Defense](/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Afghanistan) "Ministry of Defense (Afghanistan)") building followed traditional, Islamic and Western designs inspired by [the Pentagon](/wiki/The_Pentagon "The Pentagon"). Another mix of these designs appeared on the [Paghman Hill Castle](/wiki/Paghman_Hill_Castle "Paghman Hill Castle") completed in 2014.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-Architectural-190)^ Increasing numbers of high rises have been built in this period, with the Kabul Markaz tower in 2020 becoming the city's first to break the 100 metres (330 ft) tall barrier.^[\[192\]](#cite_note-193)^ The construction boom with modern [high-rises](/wiki/High-rise_building "High-rise building") throughout the 2010s had led to a major change in the city's skyline.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-ReutersHomes-192)^{#cite_ref-ReutersHomes_192-2}

  * [![Traditional hill dwellings](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Kabul_street_scene%2C_1974.jpg/444px-Kabul_street_scene%2C_1974.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kabul_street_scene,_1974.jpg "Traditional hill dwellings")  
  Traditional hill dwellings

Transportation {#Transportation}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Transportation")\]  
Further information: [Transport in Afghanistan](/wiki/Transport_in_Afghanistan "Transport in Afghanistan")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Flightline_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpeg/220px-Flightline_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpeg)](/wiki/File:Flightline_at_Kabul_International_Airport.jpeg) Flightline at [Hamid Karzai International Airport](/wiki/Kabul_International_Airport "Kabul International Airport") (Kabul International Airport), 2012

Kabul has no train service.^[\[67\]](#cite_note-andrewgrantham.co.uk-68)^{#cite_ref-andrewgrantham.co.uk_68-1}  

### Air {#Air}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Air")\]

[Kabul International Airport](/wiki/Kabul_International_Airport "Kabul International Airport") is located 25 km (16 mi) from the centre of Kabul. It is a hub to [Ariana Afghan Airlines](/wiki/Ariana_Afghan_Airlines "Ariana Afghan Airlines"), the national carrier of Afghanistan, as well as private airlines such as [Afghan Jet International](/wiki/Afghan_Jet_International "Afghan Jet International"), [East Horizon Airlines](/wiki/East_Horizon_Airlines "East Horizon Airlines"), [Kam Air](/wiki/Kam_Air "Kam Air"), [Pamir Airways](/wiki/Pamir_Airways "Pamir Airways"), and [Safi Airways](/wiki/Safi_Airways "Safi Airways"). Regional airlines such as [Air India](/wiki/Air_India "Air India"), [SpiceJet](/wiki/SpiceJet "SpiceJet"), [flydubai](/wiki/Flydubai "Flydubai"), [Emirates](/wiki/Emirates_(airline) "Emirates (airline)"), [Gulf Air](/wiki/Gulf_Air "Gulf Air"), [Mahan Air](/wiki/Mahan_Air "Mahan Air"), [Pakistan International Airlines](/wiki/Pakistan_International_Airlines "Pakistan International Airlines"), [Turkish Airlines](/wiki/Turkish_Airlines "Turkish Airlines") and others also had regularly scheduled flights to the airport.  

### Road {#Road}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Road")\]

The [AH76](/wiki/AH76 "AH76") highway (or Kabul-Charikar Highway) connected Kabul north towards [Charikar](/wiki/Charikar "Charikar"), [Pol-e Khomri](/wiki/Pol-e_Khomri "Pol-e Khomri") and [Mazar-i-Sharif](/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif "Mazar-i-Sharif") (310 km (190 mi) away), with leading roads to [Kunduz](/wiki/Kunduz "Kunduz") (250 km (160 mi) away). The [AH77](/wiki/AH77 "AH77") highway went west towards [Bamiyan Province](/wiki/Bamiyan_Province "Bamiyan Province") (150 km (93 mi) away) and [Chaghcharan](/wiki/Chaghcharan "Chaghcharan") in the central mountains of Afghanistan. To the south-west, the Kabul-Ghazni Highway went to [Ghazni](/wiki/Ghazni "Ghazni") (130 km (81 mi) away) and [Kandahar](/wiki/Kandahar "Kandahar") (460 km (290 mi) away). To the south, the Kabul-Gardez Highway connected it to [Gardez](/wiki/Gardez "Gardez") (100 km (62 mi) away) and [Khost](/wiki/Khost "Khost"). To the east, the Kabul-Jalalabad Highway went to [Jalalabad](/wiki/Jalalabad "Jalalabad") (120 km (75 mi) away) and across the border to [Peshawar](/wiki/Peshawar "Peshawar").

Much of the road network in downtown Kabul consisted of square or circle intersections (*char-rahi* ). The main square in the city was Pashtunistan Square (named after [Pashtunistan](/wiki/Pashtunistan "Pashtunistan")), which had a large [fountain](/wiki/Fountain "Fountain") in it and was located adjacent to the presidential palace, the [Central Bank](/wiki/Da_Afghanistan_Bank "Da Afghanistan Bank"), and other landmarks.^[\[193\]](#cite_note-194)^ The [Massoud Circle](/wiki/Massoud_Circle "Massoud Circle") was located by the [U.S. Embassy](/wiki/Embassy_of_the_United_States,_Kabul "Embassy of the United States, Kabul") and had the road leading to the airport. In the old city, Sar-e Chawk roundabout was at the center of Maiwand Road (*[Jadayi Maiwand](/wiki/Jadayi_Maiwand "Jadayi Maiwand")* ). Once all roads led to it, and in the 16th century was called the "navel of Kabul".^[\[194\]](#cite_note-195)^ In the [Shahr-e Naw](/wiki/Shahr-e_Naw "Shahr-e Naw") district there were several major intersections: Ansari, Haji Yaqub, Quwayi Markaz, Sedarat, and Turabaz Khan. The latter, named after [Turabaz Khan](/wiki/Turabaz_Khan "Turabaz Khan"), connected Flower Street and [Chicken Street](/wiki/Chicken_Street "Chicken Street"). There were also two major intersections in western Kabul: the [Deh Mazang](/wiki/Deh_Mazang "Deh Mazang") Circle and [Kote Sangi](/wiki/Kote_Sangi "Kote Sangi"). Salang Watt was the main road to the north-west, whereas Asamayi Watt and Seh Aqrab (also called Sevom Aqrab) was the main road to western Kabul.{#cite_ref-195}

The steep population rise in the 21st century had caused major congestion problems for the city's roads.^[\[195\]](#cite_note-196)^ In efforts to tackle this issue, a 95 km outer [ring road](/wiki/Ring_road "Ring road") costing $110 million was approved in 2017.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-197)^^[\[197\]](#cite_note-198)^ Construction would have taken five years and it will run from [Char Asiab](/wiki/Char_Asiab "Char Asiab") via [Ahmad Shah Baba Mina](/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Baba_Mina "Ahmad Shah Baba Mina"), [Deh Sabz](/wiki/Deh_Sabz "Deh Sabz") ("Kabul New City" development area), the AH76 highway, [Paghman](/wiki/Paghman "Paghman") and back to Char Asyab.^[\[198\]](#cite_note-199)^ A new bus [public transport](/wiki/Public_transport "Public transport") service was also planned to be opened in 2018 (see below).^[\[199\]](#cite_note-200)^ In September 2017, the head of the Kabul Municipality announced that 286 meters of pedestrian overpass [footbridges](/wiki/Footbridge "Footbridge") will be built in eight busy areas "in the near future".^[\[200\]](#cite_note-201)^{#cite_ref-201}

Under the Kabul Urban Transport Efficiency Improvement Project that was signed in 2014 and backed by the [World Bank](/wiki/World_Bank "World Bank"), the city has seen widespread improvements in road conditions, including the building of new pedestrian sidewalks, drainage systems, lighting and [asphalted](/wiki/Asphalt_concrete "Asphalt concrete") road surfaces. The project runs until 31 December 2019.^[\[201\]](#cite_note-202)^^[\[202\]](#cite_note-203)^{#cite_ref-203}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Afghan_National_Police_set_up_Ring_of_Steel_%284671626066%29.jpg/250px-Afghan_National_Police_set_up_Ring_of_Steel_%284671626066%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Afghan_National_Police_set_up_Ring_of_Steel_(4671626066).jpg) A [Toyota Corolla (E100)](/wiki/Toyota_Corolla_(E100) "Toyota Corolla (E100)") at a security checkpoint in 2010

Private vehicles had been on the rise in Kabul since 2002, with about 700,000 cars registered as of 2013 and up to 80% of the cars reported to be [Toyota Corollas](/wiki/Toyota_Corolla "Toyota Corolla").^[\[203\]](#cite_note-204)^^[\[204\]](#cite_note-205)^^[\[205\]](#cite_note-ABC-206)^ The number of dealerships had also increased from 77 in 2003 to over 550 by 2010.^[\[206\]](#cite_note-207)^ Gas stations were mainly private-owned. Bicycles on the road were a common sight in the city.{#cite_ref-207}  

### Public transport {#Public_transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Public transport")\]

The [taxicabs](/wiki/Taxicab "Taxicab") in Kabul were painted in a white and yellow livery. The majority of these were older model Toyota Corollas. A few Soviet-era Russian cabs were also still in operation.

Long-distance road journeys were made by private [Mercedes-Benz coach buses](/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_buses "Mercedes-Benz buses") or vans, trucks and cars. Although a nationwide bus service was available from Kabul, flying was safer, especially for foreigners. The city's public bus service ([Milli Bus](/wiki/Milli_Bus "Milli Bus") / "National Bus") was established in the 1960s to take [commuters](/wiki/Commuters "Commuters") on daily routes to many destinations. The service had about 800 buses. The Kabul bus system had discovered a new source of revenue in whole-bus advertising from [MTN](/wiki/MTN_Group "MTN Group") similar to "bus wrap" advertising on public transit in more developed nations. There was also an express bus that runs from downtown to Hamid Karzai International Airport for [Safi Airways](/wiki/Safi_Airways "Safi Airways") passengers.

An electric [trolleybus](/wiki/Trolleybus "Trolleybus") system operated in Kabul from February 1979 to 1992 using [Škoda](/wiki/%C5%A0koda_Works "Škoda Works") fleet built by a [Czechoslovak](/wiki/Czechoslovakia "Czechoslovakia") company (see [Trolleybuses in Kabul](/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Kabul "Trolleybuses in Kabul") for more). The trolleybus service was highly popular mainly due to its low price compared to the Millie Bus conventional bus service. The last trolleybus came to a halt in late 1992 due to warfare -- much of the [copper](/wiki/Copper "Copper") [overhead wires](/wiki/Overhead_line "Overhead line") were later looted but a few of them, including the steel poles, can still be seen in Kabul today.^[\[150\]](#cite_note-spvd.cz-151)^^[\[207\]](#cite_note-208)^{#cite_ref-208}

In June 2017 Kabul Municipality unveiled plans for a [new bus rapid transit](/wiki/Kabul_bus_rapid_transit "Kabul bus rapid transit") system, the first major urban public transportation scheme. It was expected to open by 2018,^[\[208\]](#cite_note-209)^^[\[209\]](#cite_note-210)^ but its construction had been hampered. In March 2021, a new city bus service was launched in Kabul using American vehicles built by [IC Bus](/wiki/IC_Bus "IC Bus"), and accompanied by newly built [bus stops](/wiki/Bus_stop "Bus stop") throughout the city. Five buses entered service on one route which is expected to be expanded to a fleet of 200 buses on 16 different routes.^[\[210\]](#cite_note-211)^^[\[211\]](#cite_note-212)^{#cite_ref-212}  

### Internet-based participatory planning {#Internet-based_participatory_planning}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Internet-based participatory planning")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/An_Open_Call_for_participation_in_Kabul_city.jpg/220px-An_Open_Call_for_participation_in_Kabul_city.jpg)](/wiki/File:An_Open_Call_for_participation_in_Kabul_city.jpg) Kabul city announced open calls through the Kabul municipality's HP and its Facebook page, to participate in town meeting and planning process [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kabul_mayor_speaking_during_solid_waste_discussion_league.png/220px-Kabul_mayor_speaking_during_solid_waste_discussion_league.png)](/wiki/File:Kabul_mayor_speaking_during_solid_waste_discussion_league.png) Kabul mayor [Mohammad Daud Sultanzoy](/wiki/Mohammad_Daud_Sultanzoy "Mohammad Daud Sultanzoy") speaking with league management during the inauguration ceremony of first ever internet-based solid waste discussion league in 2021 [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/MoU_between_Kabul_and_NITech.png/220px-MoU_between_Kabul_and_NITech.png)](/wiki/File:MoU_between_Kabul_and_NITech.png) A [memorandum of understanding](/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding "Memorandum of understanding") signed by Kabul City [mayor](/wiki/Mayor "Mayor") Ahmad Zaki Sarfaraz and [Nagoya Institute of Technology](/wiki/Nagoya_Institute_of_Technology "Nagoya Institute of Technology") [executive director](/wiki/Executive_director "Executive director") in 2019

In 2019, the [Nagoya Institute of Technology](/wiki/Nagoya_Institute_of_Technology "Nagoya Institute of Technology"), in partnership with the Kabul city Municipality, jointly agreed to deploy a digital platform, called D-Agree in urban planning to provide support for stakeholders to promote meaningful public participation and help reach consensus in Kabul city planning process.^[\[212\]](#cite_note-Un2022-213)^{#cite_ref-Un2022_213-0}

From September 2019 until the [Fall of Kabul (2021)](/wiki/Fall_of_Kabul_(2021) "Fall of Kabul (2021)") in August 2021, the platform was used on behalf of Kabul Municipality to moderate more than 300 Kabul city-related planning discussions.^[\[213\]](#cite_note-auto-214)^^[\[214\]](#cite_note-215)^ ^[\[215\]](#cite_note-216)^^[\[216\]](#cite_note-217)^ ^[\[217\]](#cite_note-218)^^[\[218\]](#cite_note-219)^ ^[\[219\]](#cite_note-220)^ In these discussions, more than 15,000 citizens participated in planning activities hosted by D-Agree and generated more than 71,000 opinions which catalogued into [issue-based information system](/wiki/Issue-based_information_system "Issue-based information system") regarding urban-related thematic areas.^[\[212\]](#cite_note-Un2022-213)^ Despite the [Taliban](/wiki/Taliban "Taliban") take-over, D-Agree will continue to play an important role in facilitating urban planning and infrastructure-related consultations.^[\[220\]](#cite_note-221)^{#cite_ref-221}

In 2022, [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") reported that D-Agree Afghanistan is used as a digital and smart city solutions in [Afghanistan](/wiki/Afghanistan "Afghanistan").^[\[212\]](#cite_note-Un2022-213)^^[\[221\]](#cite_note-Thetrans2022-222)^{#cite_ref-Thetrans2022_222-0}

D-Agree, is a discussion support platform with [artificial intelligence](/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence")--based facilitation.^[\[222\]](#cite_note-HadfiHaqbeenSahabIto2021-223)^ The discussion trees in D-Agree, inspired by [issue-based information system](/wiki/Issue-based_information_system "Issue-based information system"), contain a combination of four types of elements: issues, ideas, pros, and cons.^[\[222\]](#cite_note-HadfiHaqbeenSahabIto2021-223)^ The software extracts a discussion's structure in real time based on IBIS, automatically classifying all the sentences.^[\[222\]](#cite_note-HadfiHaqbeenSahabIto2021-223)^{#cite_ref-HadfiHaqbeenSahabIto2021_223-2}  

Education {#Education}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Education")\]  
Further information: [Education in Afghanistan](/wiki/Education_in_Afghanistan "Education in Afghanistan") and [List of schools in Kabul](/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Kabul "List of schools in Kabul")

The [Ministry of Education](/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Afghanistan) "Ministry of Education (Afghanistan)") led by [Ghulam Farooq Wardak](/wiki/Ghulam_Farooq_Wardak "Ghulam Farooq Wardak") was responsible for the education system in Afghanistan.^[\[223\]](#cite_note-224)^ [Public](/wiki/State_school "State school") and [private schools](/wiki/Private_school "Private school") in the city have reopened since 2002 after they were shut down or destroyed during fighting in the 1980s to the late 1990s. Boys and girls were strongly encouraged to attend school under the [Karzai administration](/wiki/Karzai_administration "Karzai administration") but many more schools were needed not only in Kabul but throughout the country. The [Afghan Ministry of Education](/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Afghanistan) "Ministry of Education (Afghanistan)") had plans to build more schools in the coming years so that education was provided to all citizens of the country. High schools in Kabul included:{#cite_ref-224}

* [Abdul Hadi Dawi High School](/wiki/Abdul_Hadi_Dawi_High_School "Abdul Hadi Dawi High School"), a school for boys
* Abdul Rahim-e-Shaheed High School, a school for boys and girls (up to Year 6) founded in 1970
* [Afghan Turk High Schools](/wiki/Afghan_Turk_High_Schools "Afghan Turk High Schools"), Turkish-Afghan schools
* Aisha-i-Durani School, a German-Afghan school for girls
* [Amani High School](/wiki/Amani_High_School "Amani High School"), a German-Afghan school for boys founded in 1924
* [Ghulam Haider Khan High School](/wiki/Ghulam_Haider_Khan_High_School "Ghulam Haider Khan High School"), a school for boys
* [Habibia High School](/wiki/Habibia_High_School "Habibia High School"), a British-Afghan school founded in 1903 by King [Habibullah Khan](/wiki/Habibullah_Khan "Habibullah Khan")
* [International School of Kabul](/wiki/International_School_of_Kabul "International School of Kabul"), an American-Afghan school
* [Lycée Esteqlal](/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_Esteqlal "Lycée Esteqlal"), a Franco-Afghan school founded in 1922
* [Malalai High School](/wiki/Malalai_High_School "Malalai High School"), a Franco-Afghan school for girls
* [Nazo Ana High School](/wiki/Nazo_Ana_High_School "Nazo Ana High School"), a school for boys
* [Rahman Baba High School](/wiki/Rahman_Baba_High_School "Rahman Baba High School"), an American-Afghan school for boys

### Universities {#Universities}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Universities")\]

* [Kabul Health Sciences Institute](/wiki/Kabul_Health_Sciences_Institute "Kabul Health Sciences Institute")
* [Kabul Medical University](/wiki/Kabul_Medical_University "Kabul Medical University")
* [Kabul Polytechnic University](/wiki/Kabul_Polytechnic_University "Kabul Polytechnic University")
* [Kabul University](/wiki/Kabul_University "Kabul University")

* [Salam University](/wiki/Salam_University "Salam University")

Health care {#Health_care}
--------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Health care")\]  
Further information: [Health care in Afghanistan](/wiki/Health_care_in_Afghanistan "Health care in Afghanistan") and [List of hospitals in Afghanistan](/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Afghanistan "List of hospitals in Afghanistan")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg) [Daoud Khan Military Hospital](/wiki/Daoud_Khan_Military_Hospital "Daoud Khan Military Hospital")

[Health care in Afghanistan](/wiki/Health_care_in_Afghanistan "Health care in Afghanistan") has improved in the last two decades. There are over 5,000 [hospitals and clinics](/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Afghanistan "List of hospitals in Afghanistan") in the country, with the major ones being in Kabul.

* ADEI Medical Complex^[\[224\]](#cite_note-225)^{#cite_ref-225}
* Afghan-Japan Hospital^[\[225\]](#cite_note-226)^{#cite_ref-226}
* Afshar Hospital
* Ahmad Shah Baba Hospital
* Ariana Medical Complex^[\[226\]](#cite_note-227)^{#cite_ref-227}
* [Atatürk Children's Hospital](/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_Children%27s_Hospital "Atatürk Children's Hospital")
* [CURE International Hospital](/wiki/CURE_International "CURE International")^[\[227\]](#cite_note-228)^{#cite_ref-228}
* [Daoud Khan Military Hospital](/wiki/Daoud_Khan_Military_Hospital "Daoud Khan Military Hospital")
* [French Medical Institute for Children](/wiki/French_Medical_Institute_for_Children "French Medical Institute for Children")
* [Indira Gandhi Children's Hospital](/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_Children%27s_Hospital "Indira Gandhi Children's Hospital")
* [Jamhuriat Hospital](/wiki/Jamhuriat_Hospital "Jamhuriat Hospital")
* [Jinnah Hospital](/wiki/Jinnah_Hospital,_Kabul "Jinnah Hospital, Kabul")
* Malalai Maternity Hospital
* Maywand Hospital
* Rabia-I-Balki Maternity Hospital
* Wazir Akbar Khan Hospital^[\[228\]](#cite_note-UAE_Medical_Firm_To_Run_Two_Key_Kabul_Hospitals-229)^{#cite_ref-UAE_Medical_Firm_To_Run_Two_Key_Kabul_Hospitals_229-0}

Notable people {#Notable_people}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Notable people")\]  

### Rulers {#Rulers}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Rulers")\]

* [Gaju Khan Yousafzai](/wiki/Gaju_Khan "Gaju Khan") (c. 1490--1565), Pashtun revolutionary leader who served under the banner of [Sher Shah Sur](/wiki/Sher_Shah_Suri "Sher Shah Suri") of the [Sur Empire](/wiki/Sur_Empire "Sur Empire")

### Politicians {#Politicians}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Politicians")\]

* [Sher Ali Khan](/wiki/Sher_Ali_Khan "Sher Ali Khan") (c. 1825--1879), former Emir of Afghanistan
* [Abdur Rahman Khan](/wiki/Abdur_Rahman_Khan "Abdur Rahman Khan") (born between 1840 and 1844 -- 1901), Emir of Afghanistan
* [Amanullah Khan](/wiki/Amanullah_Khan "Amanullah Khan") (1892--1960), Emir of Afghanistan during the [Independence War](/wiki/Third_Anglo-Afghan_War "Third Anglo-Afghan War") till abdication in 1929
* [Habibullāh Kalakāni](/wiki/Habibull%C4%81h_Kalak%C4%81ni "Habibullāh Kalakāni") (1891--1929), Revolutionary rebel leader and ruler of Afghanistan in 1929
* [Mohammed Zahir Shah](/wiki/Mohammed_Zahir_Shah "Mohammed Zahir Shah") (1914--2007), the last king of Afghanistan
* [Hafizullah Amin](/wiki/Hafizullah_Amin "Hafizullah Amin") (1929--1979), former Prime Minister of Afghanistan
* [Babrak Karmal](/wiki/Babrak_Karmal "Babrak Karmal") (1929--1996), former President of Afghanistan
* [Zamina Begum](/wiki/Zamina_Begum "Zamina Begum") (1917--1978), former Afghan princess and first lady of Afghanistan
* [Sibghatullah Mojaddedi](/wiki/Sibghatullah_Mojaddedi "Sibghatullah Mojaddedi") (1926--2019), former President of Afghanistan
* [Anahita Ratebzad](/wiki/Anahita_Ratebzad "Anahita Ratebzad") (1931--2014), former Minister of Social Affairs and Tourism of Afghanistan
* [Abdullah Abdullah](/wiki/Abdullah_Abdullah "Abdullah Abdullah") (born 1960), former chief executive officer of Afghanistan
* [Shukria Barakzai](/wiki/Shukria_Barakzai "Shukria Barakzai") (born 1970), Afghan politician and former ambassador of Afghanistan to Norway
* [Roya Rahmani](/wiki/Roya_Rahmani "Roya Rahmani") (born 1978), former Afghan diplomat, who served as Afghanistan's first female ambassador to the United States
* [Nasima Razmyar](/wiki/Nasima_Razmyar "Nasima Razmyar") (born 1984), Afghan-Finnish politician

### Religious figures {#Religious_figures}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Religious figures")\]

* [Abu Khalid al-Kabuli](/wiki/Abu_Khalid_al-Kabuli "Abu Khalid al-Kabuli") (live during 7th century), a prominent early Islamic figure, known for his close companionship with [Ali Zayn al Abidin](/wiki/Ali_al-Sajjad "Ali al-Sajjad"), fourth [Imam](/wiki/Imam "Imam") of [Shia Islam](/wiki/Shia_Islam "Shia Islam")
* [Abu Hanifa](/wiki/Abu_Hanifa "Abu Hanifa") (born 7th century), prominent Islamic scholar and the founder of the [Hanafi school](/wiki/Hanafi_school "Hanafi school") of jurisprudence, one of the four major [Sunni](/wiki/Sunni_Islam "Sunni Islam") legal schools, whose ancestors hailed from the Kabul region
* [Mir Zahid Harawi](/wiki/Mir_Zahid_Harawi "Mir Zahid Harawi") (born 17th century), religious scholar and historian, worked and died in Kabul
* [Mohaqiq Kabuli](/wiki/Mohaqiq_Kabuli "Mohaqiq Kabuli") (born 1928), [Twelver Shia](/wiki/Twelver_Shi%27ism "Twelver Shi'ism") [Marja](/wiki/Marja%27 "Marja'")'

### Musicians {#Musicians}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Musicians")\]

* [Mohammad Hussain Sarahang](/wiki/Mohammad_Hussain_Sarahang "Mohammad Hussain Sarahang") (1924--1983), singer
* [Abdul Rahim Sarban](/wiki/Abdul_Rahim_Sarban "Abdul Rahim Sarban") (1930--1993), singer
* [Nainawaz](/wiki/Nainawaz "Nainawaz") (1935--1979), artist, poet and composer
* [Farhad Darya](/wiki/Farhad_Darya "Farhad Darya") (born 1962), singer
* [Ahmad Zahir](/wiki/Ahmad_Zahir "Ahmad Zahir") (1946--1979), singer
* [Aryana Sayeed](/wiki/Aryana_Sayeed "Aryana Sayeed") (born 1985), singer

### Athletes {#Athletes}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Athletes")\]

* [Salim Durani](/wiki/Salim_Durani "Salim Durani") (1934--2023), former cricketer and only Indian Test cricketer to have been born in Afghanistan
* [Siyar Bahadurzada](/wiki/Siyar_Bahadurzada "Siyar Bahadurzada") (born 1984), mixed martial artist, former [Shooto](/wiki/Shooto "Shooto") Middleweight Champion, and first athlete from Afghanistan to fight in the [UFC](/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship "Ultimate Fighting Championship")
* [Asghar Afghan](/wiki/Asghar_Afghan "Asghar Afghan") (born 1987), retired cricketer, Afghanistan's former captain who ended his career with the highest T20I wins as captain
* [Omar Nazar](/wiki/Omar_Nazar "Omar Nazar") (born 1978), footballer
* [Zubayr Amiri](/wiki/Zubayr_Amiri "Zubayr Amiri") (born 1990), footballer for SC Hessen Dreieich and the Afghanistan national team
* [Karim Janat](/wiki/Karim_Janat "Karim Janat") (born 1998), cricketer, brother to [Asghar Afghan](/wiki/Asghar_Afghan "Asghar Afghan")
* [Naveen-ul-Haq](/wiki/Naveen-ul-Haq "Naveen-ul-Haq") (born 1999), cricketer
* [Hamid Rahimi](/wiki/Hamid_Rahimi "Hamid Rahimi") (born 1983), boxer

### Actors and Actresses {#Actors_and_Actresses}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Actors and Actresses")\]

* [Azita Ghanizada](/wiki/Azita_Ghanizada "Azita Ghanizada") (born 1978 or 1979), American actress
* [Leena Alam](/wiki/Leena_Alam "Leena Alam") (born 1978), film actress
* [Vida Samadzai](/wiki/Vida_Samadzai "Vida Samadzai") (born 1978), actress, model and beauty pageant titleholder
* [Annet Mahendru](/wiki/Annet_Mahendru "Annet Mahendru") (born 1985), Afghan-born American actress
* [Ahmad Khan Mahmoodzada](/wiki/Ahmad_Khan_Mahmoodzada "Ahmad Khan Mahmoodzada") (born 1997), former child actor

### Writers and Poets {#Writers_and_Poets}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Writers and Poets")\]

* [Saib Tabrizi](/wiki/Saib_Tabrizi "Saib Tabrizi") (born c. 1592) Persian poet who spent several years in Kabul under the patronage of Mirzā Aḥsan-Allāh Ẓafar Khan, the governor of Kabul at the time
* [Khaled Hosseini](/wiki/Khaled_Hosseini "Khaled Hosseini") (born 1965), Afghan-American novelist
* [Homeira Qaderi](/wiki/Homeira_Qaderi "Homeira Qaderi") (born 1980), writer
* [Nainawaz](/wiki/Nainawaz "Nainawaz") (1935--1979), artist, poet and composer

### Journalists {#Journalists}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Journalists")\]

* [Sayed Hamid Noori](/wiki/Sayed_Hamid_Noori "Sayed Hamid Noori") (born 1965), journalist
* [Mustafa Nayyem](/wiki/Mustafa_Nayyem "Mustafa Nayyem") (born 1981), Afghan-[Ukrainian](/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine") journalist who was influential in sparking the [Euromaidan](/wiki/Euromaidan "Euromaidan")
* [Yama Wolasmal](/wiki/Yama_Wolasmal "Yama Wolasmal") (born 1982), journalist
* [Farahnaz Forotan](/wiki/Farahnaz_Forotan "Farahnaz Forotan") (born 1992), journalist
* [Wahida Faizi](/wiki/Wahida_Faizi "Wahida Faizi") (born 1994), journalist

### Activists {#Activists}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kabul&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Activists")\]

* [Adela Mohseni](/wiki/Adela_Mohseni "Adela Mohseni") (born c. 1972), women's rights activist
